# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# GCC RTL Intermediate Representation Pass Chain

## Your Task

Trace how GCC's RTL (Register Transfer Language) passes are organized and executed in gcc. Find C++ source files implementing: the RTL pass class, the pass_expand (gimple to RTL), a representative RTL optimization pass, and the final code generation pass.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d, sg-evals/gcc--96dfb333.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d` (llvm/llvm-project)
- `sg-evals/gcc--96dfb333` (gcc-mirror/gcc)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I've successfully traced GCC's RTL pass chain and created a comprehensive answer file. Here's a summary of my findings:

## GCC RTL Pass Chain Summary

I've identified and documented the complete RTL (Register Transfer Language) pass infrastructure in GCC:

### Key Components Found:

1. **RTL Pass Base Class** (`gcc/tree-pass.h:126-133`)
   - `rtl_opt_pass` class extending `opt_pass`
   - Provides the framework for all RTL optimization passes

2. **GIMPLE to RTL Conversion** (`gcc/cfgexpand.cc:7010-7020`)
   - `pass_expand` class - the critical gateway between tree-based GIMPLE and RTL
   - First RTL pass that initializes RTL generation

3. **RTL Optimization Pass (Representative)** (`gcc/dse.cc:3784-3802`)
   - `pass_rtl_dse1` and `pass_rtl_dse2` classes
   - Implement Dead Store Elimination (DSE)
   - Exemplify the structure of RTL optimization passes with gate() and execute() methods

4. **Final Code Generation Pass** (`gcc/final.cc:4340-4353`)
   - `pass_final` class - the last RTL pass
   - Converts optimized RTL into final assembly code

5. **Pass Registration** (`gcc/passes.def:460-575`)
   - Shows the complete execution order of the RTL pass chain
   - `pass_expand` (line 460) → `pass_rest_of_compilation` (lines 462-575) → `pass_final` (line 572)

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file references, symbol names, and a detailed narrative explaining how GCC's RTL passes are organized and executed.

The RTL pass chain flows through four key components:\\n\\n1. **RTL Pass Base Class (gcc/tree-pass.h:126-133)**: The `rtl_opt_pass` class extends `opt_pass` and serves as the base class for all RTL optimization passes. RTL passes are distinguished from GIMPLE passes (gimple_opt_pass) by the pass type RTL_PASS. The rtl_opt_pass class provides the framework for implementing optimization passes that operate on the RTL intermediate representation, with virtual methods for gate() and execute() that subclasses override.\\n\\n2. **GIMPLE to RTL Expansion (gcc/cfgexpand.cc:7010-7020)**: The `pass_expand` class converts GIMPLE code to RTL. This is the critical gateway between the tree-based GIMPLE representation and the register-transfer RTL representation. The pass_expand::execute() method (line 7023) calls rewrite_out_of_ssa() and initializes RTL generation, making it the first RTL pass in the compilation pipeline.\\n\\n3. **RTL Optimization Passes - Representative Example (gcc/dse.cc:3784-3802 and 3827-3845)**: The `pass_rtl_dse1` and `pass_rtl_dse2` classes exemplify RTL optimization passes. These implement Dead Store Elimination (DSE) on the RTL, with gate() methods controlling execution based on flags (flag_dse, dbg_cnt) and execute() methods calling rest_of_handle_dse(). Multiple RTL optimization passes run in sequence within pass_rest_of_compilation, including pass_rtl_fwprop, pass_cse, pass_combine, pass_ira, pass_reload, and others shown in passes.def lines 464-574.\\n\\n4. **Final Code Generation Pass (gcc/final.cc:4340-4353)**: The `pass_final` class implements the final code generation phase. As the last RTL pass (passes.def:572), it executes rest_of_handle_final(), which generates the final assembly code from the optimized RTL. This pass is responsible for converting RTL instructions into actual target machine code.\\n\\nThe pass execution order defined in gcc/passes.def shows the critical flow: pass_expand (line 460) converts GIMPLE to RTL, then pass_rest_of_compilation (lines 462-575) encapsulates all RTL optimizations and code generation, concluding with pass_final (line 572) that emits the final assembly output.\"\n}\n",

RTL passes are distinguished from GIMPLE passes (gimple_opt_pass) by the pass type RTL_PASS. The rtl_opt_pass class provides the framework for implementing optimization passes that operate on the RTL intermediate representation, with virtual methods for gate() and execute() that subclasses override.\\n\\n2. **GIMPLE to RTL Expansion (gcc/cfgexpand.cc:7010-7020)**: The `pass_expand` class converts GIMPLE code to RTL. This is the critical gateway between the tree-based GIMPLE representation and the register-transfer RTL representation. The pass_expand::execute() method (line 7023) calls rewrite_out_of_ssa() and initializes RTL generation, making it the first RTL pass in the compilation pipeline.\\n\\n3. **RTL Optimization Passes - Representative Example (gcc/dse.cc:3784-3802 and 3827-3845)**: The `pass_rtl_dse1` and `pass_rtl_dse2` classes exemplify RTL optimization passes. These implement Dead Store Elimination (DSE) on the RTL, with gate() methods controlling execution based on flags (flag_dse, dbg_cnt) and execute() methods calling rest_of_handle_dse(). Multiple RTL optimization passes run in sequence within pass_rest_of_compilation, including pass_rtl_fwprop, pass_cse, pass_combine, pass_ira, pass_reload, and others shown in passes.def lines 464-574.\\n\\n4. **Final Code Generation Pass (gcc/final.cc:4340-4353)**: The `pass_final` class implements the final code generation phase. As the last RTL pass (passes.def:572), it executes rest_of_handle_final(), which generates the final assembly code from the optimized RTL.
